text:
Delicious and moist! I made some changes to the recipe; I added 1 cup milk, 1 cup chips, 1 cup sugar, 1/2 cup oil, and some vanilla essence. With the sugar topping, they were plenty sweet. Only problem was there was way too much batter for 12 muffins; I ended up making two trays and they were done in 18 minutes. I give it four stars only because of all the changes I had to make; otherwise it would be five!

text:
I have been using this recipe for a year now and it is my "official" chocolate chip muffin mix.  By making some very simple alterations, I've had some really wonderful results.  First, to combat dryness, I add the amount of 3/4 cup of milk AND 1/4 cup of sour cream. Not enough moistness for you?  I've gone as much as 1/2 cup of the sour cream and been happy with it--depends on your tastes.  I also add a teaspoon of vanilla extract into the batter, which lends a great flavor.  I love the topping of sugars, but they are also wonderful with coarse sugar sprinkled on the top.  It's a simple recipe that yields consistant results.  My daughters love these muffins and request them often.

text:
While it usually drives me crazy when reviewers go tinkering around with recipes, I thought this was a good one.  As an experienced baker, though, one usually creams the wet ingredients with the sugar and then adds the dry...which is what I did.  I blended the oil, 1 cup of milk, egg (and I added some vanilla) in my Kitchenaid...then added the dry ingredients and hand-stirred in the chips.  The sugar on top was a nice touch and my muffins came out just fine.  I'd definitely make these again.  If you don't use cupcake liners, don't bake these as long...the sugar will burn along the sides of the muffin pan.

text:
Delicious! Just like the ones I used to buy at a gourmet coffee shop in San Diego.   Per some of the other reviews, I added more milk--about 1 cup total. I like the crunchy goodness of the sugar baked on top, but found that I didn't need nearly as much as the recipe called for. The Results were satisfying with just half the amount of sugar sprinkled on top (though I did not cut the amount of sugar in the actual batter). I like the mini chips and would probably not make these with full-size ones since the chocolate seems well dispersed with the mini chips. Mine were done in exactly 20 minutes.  The recipe was easy to follow, used ingredients most cooks would already have on hand, and the results were delicious. This is a keeper!

text:
Very good muffin recipe!!  I was wanting to make chocolat chocolate chip muffins, but couldnt find a decent one on this site.  So I made the following adjustments: 1/3 cup unsweetened cocoa powder added to 1 2/3 cup flour to equal a total of 2 cups as recipes lists.  1 cup milk rather than 3/4 cup(I used evaporated milk since thats what I had on hand), and 1 1/2 tsp vanilla extract.  I also left off the sugar topping.  As the directions state, it is VERY VERY important to never over mix a muffin or any quick bread batter.  This will cause it to be tough once baked.  I mix just until incorporated, lumps are OK, they will bake out in the oven.  I also recommend buying a commercial portion scoop for making muffins and cupcakes.  Theyre no more than $10 and your muffins/cupcakes will come out even and same sized.  The scoop to look for typicaly has a blue handle and is known as #16 scoop (for a standard sized muffin tin), or food dipper.  They look like an ice cream scoop.  I bought mine for $5.  And I use it every tiime I make muffins or cupcakes.  I also use a #30 (black handle) for perfect size cookies!

text:
I'm rating these four stars. These muffins are YUMMY! But the baking time is off. Many reviews say to shorten the baking time so I did. I set my timer for 15 minutes and I think they would have been perfect at around 13 minutes. I have an oven thermometer so I can say pretty confidently that the given time is most definitely off. The other two changes I made were to add 1/4 cup of light sour cream to help with any dryness issues. I also added some sprinkles to the batter and to the top of the muffins because, as my 5 year old likes to say, sprinkles make everything better :) I love the sugar topping but I had a lot left over so next time I will cut that in half. Thanks for sharing this recipe!

With a few alterations, following on the suggestions of other reviewers, these muffins were moist and FABULOUS! Even my nanny who doesn't like chocolate thought they were great. 

The alterations I made are as follows: 2/3 cup of raw sugar (we don't have processed white sugar here in Uganda so I always use raw), 1 cup milk, just under 2/3 cup oil, 2 eggs, 100g chocolate bar (smashed into pieces). I also didn't use the topping, but will try raw sugar next time.

text:
The only reason I didn't give this recipe 5 stars is that I had to alter the recipe to make them moist and tasty.  If you make this recipe as it is written you will be sorry and end up with dry crumbly muffins.   Here's what I did and I recommend you do the same.  Use 1 cup of milk, 1/2 cup vegetable oil, and a 1/2 tsp of vanilla.  If you follow those measurements, you will end up with a moist flavorful muffin.  Make sure you spray your muffin tin well.  And the side of the tin too, not just the bottom.  I used regular sized chocolate chips since that was all I had and they worked well in the recipe.

text:
I made a few changes to these too.  To the original ingredients, I added 1/4 cup skim milk (for a total of 1 cup skim milk), 1/2 cup unsweetened cocoa, 1 cup Splenda, 1/3 cup unsweetened applesauce, and 1 tsp vanilla extract.  I substituted the egg with 1/2 cup Egg Beaters (the equivalent of 2 eggs) and used whole wheat flour instead of white.  I also omitted the topping.  The results were fantastic!  The muffins actually taste like the not-so-good for you versions you can buy at coffeehouses and grocery stores.  Even my very picky daughter loves them!

CHOCOLATE CHOCOLATE CHIP MUFFIN THATS SUPER
------------------------------------------------------------

ADD 1 TSP. VANILLA ---

2 GHIRADELLI BITTER SWEET CHIPS TO EACH MUFFIN ---

CHANGED CHIPS TO 3/4 CUP MINI & REGULAR CHIPS ---

ADD 1/2 CUP  COCOA ---

CHANGED MILK TO 1 CUP ---

CHANGED SUGAR TO 3/4 CUP ---

SPRINKLE WHITE SUGAR ON TOP OF EACH BEFORE BAKING ---

NO BROWN SUGAR NEEDED ...

COOKED ABOUT 20 MINUTES 400 DEGREES ...

ENJOY !!!!

text:
I thought these muffins were just ok. I did change the recipe slightly by adding in 1/4 cup sour cream and 1 tsp. vanilla extract. Also increased the chocolate chips to 1 cup and used regular size instead of mini since that's what I had on hand. The muffins looked and smelled great when they came out of the oven. As they cooled they became a little hard on the outside and the sugar topping cracked and started breaking off to reveal a pale (but fully cooked) muffin top underneath. I think that sprinkling coarse sugar crystals on top would probably be a better alternative. When I tasted a muffin I immediately noticed it was not sweet enough and had a little bit of a floury taste. I will try to make these again, but next time I will increase the sugar that goes into the batter and leave off the sugar topping. I'm not sure the sour cream I added really did anything as far as flavor or moistness goes, so I will leave it out next time.

text:
Not bad at all.  This is an easy, basic muffin recipe that can be adjusted to anyone's taste.  I noticed a few people said it was bland and not sweet enough.  Any sweeter and I think you start getting into cupcake territory.  The first time I made it I pretty much followed the recipe to the letter except for adding a bit more milk.  I tried it again today (still have half a bag of chocolate chips burning a hole in my cupboard) and I changed it up a bit.  I stuck with 1 cup of milk, added an extra egg and changed the the 1/2 cup white sugar to 1/4 cup white, 1/4 cup brown. I also included 1 tsp of vanilla. I left off the topping this time as well due to the extra 1/4 cup of sugar added in the mixture.  I'm sure they'll go fast at breakfast in the morning!

text:
BEST chocolate chip muffin recipe yet! The key to get them very moist and not dry is to take it out earlier than it is fully baked. If you wait until the inside is completely cooked, the rest of the muffin will turn out dry. It is a great morning meal or a pick me up throughout the day. I really liked the brown sugar topping on top, it made it a little more interesting and yummy! :) I will be using this recipe from now on for muffins!

This was a good recipe, but I had to make some changes to make it better... I used 3/4 cup of light brown sugar instead of white, used 1 cup of skim milk, 3/4 cup canola oil, added 1 tsp vanilla extract, baking soda, an extra egg, some buttermilk (powder), and a full cup of dark chocolate chunks (which ended up in the bottom of the muffin so I wouldn't recommend using them for this recipe). I also replaced the glaze with melted dark chocolate and poured some on top of every muffin because they still weren't chocolatey enough and decorated them with nonpareils. I also changed the cooking time to 15 minutes. Everyone in my family enjoyed them and the 18 muffins I made were gone before the next morning. Thanks!

I read through the reviews before making these muffins and I'm glad I did. I increased the milk to a full cup (and I also used buttermilk) and I added one teaspoon of vanilla. I did use whole wheat white flour in this recipe. These were easy enough and the kids thought chocolate chip muffins were great but my husband remarked that it needs more of the chocolate chips. He thought using the mini chips was a great idea, it just needs more. I'm really glad I added more liquid because if I hadn't, these would have been really dry. Mine weren't really dry but they weren't moist, either. Good recipe, but needs a little tweaking.

I became a member just to rate this recipe! These are very yummy, and I didn't really think they would compare to a chocolate chip cookie, but they do. Instead of milk I used vanilla soy milk (a friend of mine left it at the house so I thought I'd try it instead of wasting it) and you would never know. I also put 1/2 whole wheat flour. It worked so well, I am considering buying the Vanilla soy milk just to keep the fat and cholesterol down every time I make this!

text:
Great muffins..BUT! I added one cup of milk, 2 tablespoons of hersheys unsweetened cocoa, 1 teasponn of vanilla and 1/3 cup of sugar ( I try use to use less sugar in everything). I also added almost 3/4 semi-sweet choco chips and cooked them at 400 degrees for 16-17 minutes. Any longer and they would burn. They came out great! not too sweet as the chocolate cocoa and chips really gave it flavor! I didn't top it off with sugar as it's way too much sugar for me...use more cocoa for a darker look:)

I'm glad I read the reviews before I made this. It definitely requires alteration because for a second there I thought I was making cookies because the batter was quite dry.    I used 1 cup of butter milk, 1 cup of choc chips (I would add more next time), Vanilla essence & 1/2 a cup of canola oil.    Once cooled down they were sweet enough and moistness was just right. Baked them for around 20 minutes. The sugar at the top was a nice crunchy addition. I would definitely add up to 1.5 cups of choc chips next time because I found it to be quite barren.

text:
Made a few changes, like others, and these came out incredibly good, with a dense, coffee-shop muffin texture and a delicious taste. Very moist, too. Made 16 medium sized muffins.

For the flour, used 1 cup all purpose and 1 cup whole wheat, plus 1/4 cup wheat germ. Used 1/2 cup dark brown sugar instead of white (extra moisture and more flavor). Instead of milk (I always bake non-dairy for allergy and kosher reasons), I used 1/2 cup chocolate soy milk and 3/4 cup regular soymilk. Used 2 eggs and only 1/4 cup canola oil, and added 2 tsp vanilla extract and about 1 and 1/2 tsp cinnamon. And about a cup of regular non-dairy chocolate chips. My husband isn't usually a big muffin fan, and he couldn't stop raving about this one. And the sugar topping was a nice addition, though it really didn't need any more sweetness. Baked for 19 minutes at 200 Celsius, middle rack.

Based on other reviews, I made some changes.  I used 1c milk, 2 eggs, 1/2c sour cream and 1 Tbsp vanilla.  This made the batter a little too loose, so I tossed the chocolate chips with an extra 1/c flour before stirring them into the batter. I got 18 regular sized muffins from this amount of batter.   I baked them for exactly 20 minutes and they were perfect.  They rose beautifully and were lightly brown and crispy on top.  Moist and delicious inside.  I only gave the recipe 4 stars since I made so many changes.

text:
My 3-year old daughter wanted to help fix breakfast this morning, but I didn't have any prepackaged mixes on hand. I chose this recipe because it used ingredients I had on hand, seemed quick, and had a high rating after many reviews.

I followed the advice of previous reviews and increased the milk to 1 cup. I kept everything else the same, except I used mini-muffin cups. Baking at 400 degrees for 10 minutes yielded perfect results.

My entire family enjoyed this breakfast treat. The muffins were soft and sweet!

One thing I would note: several people mentioned leaving off the topping. I think that the batter would not have been sweet enough on its own. I was tempted to add sugar after tasting it, but didn't. The sugar topping remedied this in the final product. If you plan to leave the topping off, I would add a little sugar to the batter. If you add sugar and use the topping, you'll probably find it too sweet.

Thanks for a quick and easy recipe!

text:
If you follow this recipe as written, you will have lousy muffins.  I think the only reason it rated so well is that nearly everyone is changing it.  The ingredients listed will make a very dry muffin.  The baking time will burn them.  I followed the many suggestions to increase the milk and oil and add vanilla extract.  I also baked them for 15 minutes instead of whats listed.  They turned out just ok.  Ive had such great results from all the highly rated All Recipes recipes that Ive tried, that I was expecting a really delicious muffin.  They were a bit on the dry side still and just not much flavor.  Great for dunking in coffee but thats about it. With the changes suggested, they are a solid 3 stars.  But as written its barely a 1 star.  I think recipes should be rated based on how they are written.

None
text:
I didn't quite care for THIS PARTICULAR Chocolate Chip muffin recipe. Upon preparing, things seemed "ok," but as a very experienced cook AND pretty darn good baker, I was disappointed with how "dense" and dry this recipe was and it also wasn't too sweet. Mind you, muffins don't have to be SO terribly sweet they are almost sickening. However, these were bland. Even with the chips. 
If I had to rate them on a scale of one to ten, ten being super delicious, I'd give them a two. 
They "looked" okay. But I wanted to bite into them and taste the goodness. I thought the ingredients, while simple, weren't "enough" in volume for the moisture and flavor these "dry mounds" needed. 
MY suggestions would be to add at least A HALF CUP of OIL, One Tsp of Vanilla Extract. In addition, approximately 1/3 cup MORE of milk (that, could be added in a bit at a time, but should be fine). In addition, being these are Chocolate Chip Muffins, more are needed; about 1/2 cup more, at least. You can also add a bit of grated orange zest, for a tasty addition (up to 2 tsp). Combine all the ingredients as directed. Watch time in oven. Don't overbake.

This is a mini muffin ideal recipe as-is! 

Followed the recipe as is, did one batch cupcake and another mini muffin. This muffin recipe is perfect for mini muffins, without alterations, the muffins have the expected pockets of air, they rise to the ideal size. 
The dough is heavy for a larger size muffin (cupcake or bigger), thats why amounts of liquids need to increase.

I read some reviews before I made these so I went with some of the popular substitutions. I used 1 cup of milk, 1/2 cup of oil, 1 cup of sugar, a teaspoon of vanilla extract, and a little over 1 cup of regular chocolate chips (because we love chocolate and I was out of mini chips).  With the alterations, I had enough to make 18 muffins, which I cooked for 20 minutes.  They taste delicious, my only complaint is all the chips sunk to the bottom. I dont know if that would happen with mini chips. Either way, theyre a hit in my house and I will be making them again, hopefully with the right chips!

text:
This is an awesome muffin recipe. I did follow the lead of some of the other reviewers and increased the milk and chocolate chips to 1 cup each. I also decreased the amount of sugar used to 1/2 cup and added 1/2 cup of Splenda. I suffer with Hashimoto's disease, so I am mindful of my sugar intake. I also added 1 1/2 tsp of vanilla, and left off the sugary topping. The batter actually makes 14 good sized muffins instead of 12 which was a plus for me. My muffins were done after 22 minutes of baking. This recipe took very little time out of my busy day, and was a breeze to make. The best thing about this muffin recipe is how easy it is to modify in terms of how much sugar you use. I already have this recipe tucked away in my special kitchen drawer, and it will definitely be used again and again.

text:
I will start off by saying that I'm writing this review while lying in bed with my foot in a cast. Okay that's a joke , but you definitely don't want to drop one of these "muffins" on your feet. We made these this morning and followed the recipe with no changes. We did use white chocolate chips if you consider that a change. The recipe calls for 3 teaspoons of baking powder which was the first sign that this recipe wasn't going to turn out well. Also the milk and oil amounts  seemed off according to how much flour the recipe calls for. The batter was very thick. It was very close to being the consistency of bread dough. The directions state that the "muffins" should be baked for at least 20 minutes at 400 degrees. These took over 20 minutes. I never have to bake muffins for more than 15 minutes. This recipe takes longer due to the batter being so thick. So what you end up with is a very dry, dense muffin. It was also lacking in taste other than the saltiness due the 3 teaspoons of baking powder it calls for. If you're wanting a sweet, moist muffin I would suggest skipping this recipe. Even with additional wet ingredients they would probably still taste very bland.

text:
Delicious potential ! I bumped oil and milk up and was a little heavy handed on the chocolate chips. Also added about a teaspoon of vanilla extract. 

My only complaint is that I should have gone with my gut and not baked at such a high temp. The bottoms burned at 17 minutes. The only time I start a muffin that high is corn,where I give it a nice crisp top at 400 then kick it down to 350. I kicked this one down to about 380 at the 10 minute mark and opened the door to rotate and cool the oven,alas too late.  Next time ( which there will be ) I will go 5 min at 400 then kick it down to 350.

text:
I gave this recipe 5 stars as it's such an easy recipe to work with. I did make a few changes as suggested by others. 

I added 1/4 cup more of milk and 1/4 cup of sour cream. Love the sour cream! I added 1/2 tbs of vanilla extract. When making these, I mixed the flour, salt and baking powder together. I added it to the other ingredients as I prefer to mix sugars with the wet ingredients. And, I added the chocolate chips last. We love chocolate so I doubled the chips. 

I baked them for 20 minutes and they were perfect. I think cook time depends on your oven. 

I particularly loved the sugar topping. It added some sweetness as the muffins aren't super sweet. And it also added a slight crunch. Husband and kids love them. I'll be making more soon. :-)

This recipe is ok. I did up the milk to 1 cup and add 1 teaspoon vanilla extract. As for the 3 tablespoons sugar & 2 tablespoons brown sugar - I think that's way too much topping for 12 muffins. I only used about 1/3 of it. I think 1 & 1 would be a better ratio. Next time I will add the extra 2 tablespoons sugar to the batter. After eating these I also agree with some of the other people, there is "something" missing from these muffins. I can't quite put my finger on it but I'm thinking a mashed up banana in the batter would be good. It would provide some extra sweetness. And as for the dryness, it wasn't as bad as others have suggested, but next time I will use yogurt instead of oil. That usually helps a lot. All in all, good. But would be better with a few changes next time. (Oh and, 19 minutes was perfect.)

text:
Great recipe. Like other reviewers I made some additions to suit the personal tastes of myself and my family but the basic listed recipe works well. I upped the granulated sugar in the batter to 2/3 of a cup. I like puff :) so I upped the baking powder to 4tsp. I kept the milk at 3/4 of a cup but then added 1/4 of a cup water which lightened the finished muffin. Oil was also upped to 1/2 cup and I did 2 eggs instead of one for airiness and fluff. I finished with a few chips (regular size) on the top plus a sprinkle of granulated sugar. A lot of changes! I know, but this is after making the recipe several times on separate occasions with the first time being as listed. Great five star starter recipe though with plenty of room for switching things up or tweaking.

text:
I was looking for an oil rather than butter recipe for muffins and found this terrific and easy one - a breeze to put together, and so tasty! I'm sure this could be adapted for blueberry or other add-ins. I have made it with white flour, but last time I used olive oil, palm sugar, and Trader Joe's gluten-free flour - surprisingly, they turned out great. I didn't have such high hopes for the gluten-free flour itself but they were delicious. Palm sugar just has a lower glycemic index than white sugar, but it does tend to dry out the baked goods, being less moist than regular sugar. I used the full cup of milk as other reviewers noted, and despite these major substitutions with the flour and sugar, the end result was golden brown on top, moist and fluffy inside. In fact I am going to make these again right now for a Sunday morning treat!

These were great! I followed some of the others' advice in the reviews and adjusted the milk to 1 cup, and used 2/3 cup of melted butter instead of the oil, I think it gave it a richer taste. Also, eliminated the sprinkled sugar on top and baked them as mini muffins. They were done in 15-18 minutes depending on how brown you like them. I do think that next time I'll add that 1/2 to 1 teaspoon of vanilla extract, I think it might be what's missing. Other than that I will definitely use this recipe again.

Gave it four stars because they were great after following other reviewers suggestions.  Have done these a few times now for kids school.  Increased milk to 1 cup, sugar to 3/4 cup and 1 cup of mini chips, 2 tbs vanilla, skipped the sugar on top.  I have also replaced oil with bananas and/or applesauce with success. For me, baked at 375 for 18 minutes for mini muffins and 22 minutes for big ones.  I like this because I usually have the ingredients on hand, it's simple and quick for kids as snacks or to take to school.  Thanks Janice!

text:
Great recipe! I did alter as well but I gave 5 stars because I didn't try it without alterations. I used 3/4 cup of milk, 1/4 cup of sour cream, 3/4 cup of sugar and 1 cup of chocolate chips. The muffin batter was delicious and personally I'd cut back on the chocolate chips, too much chocolate to me. I did the topping but added 1/2 a tablespoon of cinnamon to the sugar mixture and that was delicious! I didn't change the oil and I only had 3/4 cup of sugar because I don't like things too sweet. I thought the muffin was perfect in sweetness. I also dont own a muffin pan and made these in coffee mugs! I filled these 2/3 full and placed them in a pan with approximately 1.5 cups of water. The steam keeps them moist. You need to grease the cups (I use butter and a spoon to spread it around in the mug). Exactly 25 minutes and they were perfect. Very cute way to serve to guests. These mugs are small and only hold about a cup of liquid by the way. I also live at a high altitude but I didn't change anything just watched the time (started with 15 since everyone was saying their cooked at 18 and added a few min at a time) and at 25 min used a toothpick to check centers and they were done. Many people say use oven safe mugs, mine are old and I have no idea if they are, I just tested one first and no cracking occurred and so I used all. Made 6 muffins and used all the batter if the mugs are all the same set/size like mine. I did notice one mug still says microwave/dishwasher safe.

I added 1 teaspoon of real vanilla and increased the milk to 1 cup.  Also, I didn't have any all-purpose, so I used 1 cup white-wheat flour, and 1 cup whole-wheat flour. They were ever-so-slightly dry, but I I know this was caused by the wheat. I just warmed them up in the microwave and the melted chocolate chips were enough to return moisture to them, and they really were so good! My son even called them cake! This is definitely going to be my standard chocolate-chip muffin recipe from now on!

text:
I originally found this recipe titled as "Noras chocolate chip muffins" but one of the reviewers noted this link, which leads me to believe this may be the original.. Anyway, like many reviewers have said, I used 1 cup milk instead of 3/4, and would probably use a *little* more oil next time.  Substituted reg-sized semisweet choc morsels instead of minis, and the muffins still came out great - no "sunk to the bottom" problems.  I ended up with about half of my brown-white sugar mixture leftover, so I would suggest mixing 2 tbsp white sugar and 1 tbsp brown sugar... or whatever smaller 2:1 ratio mixture you'd like to adjust the sugary topping to.  Spray your tins with Pam (with Flour for Baking) and give another quick shot into each paper liner for super easy removal of these delish muffins.   This recipe is a keeper!

Used a heaping quarter cup of white sugar and a firmly packed 1/4 cup of brown sugar. 3. Used 1/2 c canola oil; added an extra splash of milk. 4. Added 1 tsp. vanilla extract. 5. Stirred batter to combine, less than 20 strokes.  Then let the batter sit for about 10 minutes. 6. Added a streusel topping instead of the sugar sprinkle. 7. Reduced baking time to 15 minutes.  Despite the reduced baking time, the muffins were still overdone and consequently a little dry.  But it's close... Next time I will try reducing the baking temperature (to 350 deg; 400 seems high to me) and watching the time very closely.

text:
I halved the recipe to make 6 muffins, enough for 2 each for breakfast.  They were on the smaller side in comparison to muffins I've made previously, but still enjoyable.  I worked them out to be 198 calories each when using the following: 5 oz sifted white flour, 50g sugar, 1.5 teaspoons baking powder, 1/4 teaspoon salt, 1/3 + 1 T skim milk, 2 T oil, 1.5 T egg, 30g chocolate chips, 6 teaspoons unpacked brown sugar for sprinkling on top.  Mine cooked for 19 minutes and barely filled 6 muffin cups 2/3 full, but they did rise up well.
